Software MSI Controller (SMSIC) Proposal of Work

Guo Ren
  • All Messages By This Member
Mar 12   #822  

Proposer

Name: GUO Ren
Organization/Affiliation: Alibaba Damo Academy, XuanTie

Introduction

The Software-interrupt MSI Controller (SMSIC) is an optional RISC-V hardware component tightly coupled to each hart, with one instance per hart. It receives incoming Message-Signaled Interrupts (MSIs) destined for a hart's software interrupt line and updates the corresponding pending bits in CSR_MIP.MSIP, CSR_SIP.SSIP, CSR_VSIP.SSIP, and CSR_HIP.VSSIP. Like the IMSIC, the SMSIC provides one or more memory-mapped registers within the system address space to receive these software MSIs without introducing new CSRs.

Comparison: IMSIC v.s. SMSIC
  • IMSIC: Dedicated to receiving MSIs and raising External Interrupt as defined in the RISC-V Privileged Specification. The MSI value contains the External Interrupt Identity (EIID), which ranges from 0 to 2047.
  • SMSIC: Dedicated to sending & receiving Software Interrupts as defined in the RISC-V Privileged Specification. The MSI value is used to set the emit policy, not EIID, before putting the MSI on the interconnect.

Why Existing Extensions Are Insufficient?

The AIA specification introduces only the MSI solution for the External Interrupt, called the Incoming MSI Controller (IMSIC).
From the ISA view, there is no MSI solution for Software Interrupt as defined in the RISC-V Privileged Specification.

Definitions

  • SMSIC - Software MSI Controller
  • IMSIC - Incoming MSI Controller
  • AIA - Advanced Interrupt Architecture
  • MSI - Message Signaled Interrupt
  • EIID - External Interrupt Identity
  • IPI - Inter-Processor Interrupts
  • RES - Rescheduling Interrupts
  • CAL - Function Call Interrupts

Background

Inter-Processor Interrupts (IPIs) are primarily used for synchronization and signal delivery among multiprocessors. Their main types include Rescheduling Interrupts (RES), Function Call Interrupts (CAL), and TLB Shootdown Interrupts. IPIs exhibit distinctly different characteristics compared to external device interrupts: IPIs scale with the number of harts, whereas external device interrupts are determined by the I/O request frequency. Empirical studies indicate that in multi-core server environments, IPIs often constitute the majority of the interrupt load. For instance, on a 96-core server under continuous stable operation, the cumulative IPI count (approximately 64.5 billion) was about 3.8 times that of external interrupts (approximately 17 billion); under specific stress test scenarios (such as ipi-bench [1]), this ratio can even reach 100:1. Furthermore, driver polling mechanisms under I/O-intensive workloads lead to a further reduction in the number of external interrupts. In conclusion, given the behavioral differences between IPIs and external interrupts in large-scale multi-core systems, it is recommended to distinguish between them at the ISA level to facilitate targeted microarchitecture-level optimizations.
The RISC-V Privileged Architecture Specification distinguishes interrupt types at the ISA level by defining dedicated software interrupts for IPIs. Similarly, the ARM Generic Interrupt Controller (GIC) employs a design that uses Software Generated Interrupts (SGIs)—separate from Locality-specific Peripheral Interrupts (LPIs)—to handle IPIs. However, the RISC-V Advanced Interrupt Architecture (AIA) specification departs from this strategy. It relies exclusively on the IMSIC for unified interrupt handling, merging IPIs into the same 2,048-interrupt-source pool as external interrupts. This design makes it difficult for the microarchitecture to distinguish IPIs, thereby hindering targeted optimizations based on IPI-specific characteristics.
During IPI-bench testing, we observed that IPI traffic imposes significant pressure on the SoC's Network-on-Chip (NoC). Since each IPI trigger generates an MSI I/O write transaction, these transactions cannot benefit from cache-coherence protocol optimizations (e.g., coalescing) and must adhere to strict ordering constraints, making it challenging for the NoC to apply performance optimizations. Particularly in cross-die and cross-socket scenarios, IPI transmissions consume substantial flow-control credits, causing backpressure and congestion at the Chip-to-Chip Gateway (CCG). Therefore, implementing IPI coalescing and merging mechanisms to reduce the quantity of IPIs is highly desirable. However, deploying interrupt coalescing and forwarding logic within the NoC incurs nontrivial hardware overhead that scales linearly with the number of interrupt sources. Because IPIs are multiplexed across the same pool of 2,048 external interrupt sources, the system cannot efficiently identify and optimize IPIs in isolation, resulting in prohibitively high overall optimization costs.
During IPI-bench testing, we observed that IPIs' batch-processing capability is crucial for broadcast scenarios, such as TLB shootdowns. Linux leverages the ipi_send_mask() interface to send IPIs to multiple CPUs in a single operation, effectively reducing interrupt overhead. This is also a typical approach of ISA and software co-optimization. Unfortunately, the IMSIC architecture defined in the RISC-V AIA specification lacks corresponding performance optimizations for such interfaces.
[1]: https://github.com/bytedance/kvm-utils/tree/master/microbenchmark/ipi-bench

Objectives

This Task Group (TG) will define the Software MSI Controller (SMSIC) extension, an optional RISC-V hardware component closely coupled with a hart, with one SMSIC per hart. An SMSIC processes both incoming and outgoing MSIs for software interrupts as defined in the RISC-V Privileged Specification.
  1. Investigate the Interrupt File design of the SMSIC (Software Message-Signaled Interrupt Controller) for receiving and processing incoming software Message Signaled Interrupts (MSIs).
  2. Investigate the doorbell-trigger mechanism of the SMSIC that emits outgoing software Message Signaled Interrupts (MSIs).
  3. Investigate a virtualization solution.
Here is a draft version of the design:
https://lists.riscv.org/g/tech-privileged/topic/117343728

RISC-V SMSIC（软件MSI控制器）提案旨在为处理器间中断（IPI）提供专门的硬件支持。该提案指出，现有AIA规范仅通过IMSIC处理外部中断，而IPI在大型多核系统中占主导地位且具有不同特性。SMSIC将为每个硬件线程提供独立的软件中断处理机制，支持虚拟化解决方案，并优化IPI的批量处理和性能。
